n Procedure
n Mesh or Loop Currents
   mesh is used because of the similarity in appearance between the closed
   network and a wire mesh fence. One can view the circuit as a “window
 the meshes as the “windows.” A mesh is a closed pathway with no other
way within it. A loop is also a closed pathway, but a loop may have other
ways within it. Therefore, all meshes are loops, but all loops are not meshes.
  , the loop made by the closed path BCDAB (Fig. 1.9) is not a mesh because it
   closed paths: BCAB and CDAC.
rrents I1 and I2 are drawn in the clockwise direction in each window (Fig.
oop current or mesh current is a fictitious current that enables us to obtain the
 h currents more easily. The number of loop currents required is always equal
er of windows of the network. This assures that the resulting equations are all
 . Loop currents may be drawn in any direction, but assigning a clockwise
all of them simplifies the process of writing equations.
ate the Polarities within Each Loop
polarities to agree with the assumed direction of the loop currents and the passive
 ion. The polarities across R3 are the opposite for each loop current. The polari-
d E2 are unaffected by the direction of the loop currents passing through them.

NIN’S THEOREM
 the value of the current IL through the resistor RL in the dc network of Fig.
ng Thevenin’s theorem.
nin’s theorem states: Any two-terminal linear network containing resistances
es of emf and current may be replaced by a single source of emf in series with a
istance. The emf of the single source of emf, called ETh, is the open-circuit emf
work terminal. The single-series resistance, called RTh, is the resistance between
 rk terminals when all of the independent sources are replaced by their internal
 s.
ion Procedure
 culate the Thevenin Voltage (Fig. 1.14b)
 the Thevenin equivalent circuit is determined for a network, the process is
 “thevenizing” the circuit.

 alculations. This problem solved the same circuit as in Fig. 1.14a. It is often
 t or necessary to have a voltage source (Thevenin equivalent) rather than a current
 orton equivalent) or a current source rather than a voltage source. Figure 1.16
 source conversion equations which indicate that a Thevenin equivalent circuit can
 d by a Norton equivalent circuit, and vice versa, provided that the following equa-
  sed: RN  RTh; ETh  IN RTh  IN RN, and IN  ETh /RN  ETh /RTh. The conversion
 hevenin and Norton equivalents is generally known as a source transformation.

S OF POWER IN AN AC CIRCUIT
al watts, total VARS, and total volt-amperes in the ac circuit of Fig. 1.29a.
watts, VARS, and volt-amperes are all dimensionally the same, that is, the
 oltage and current. However, we use the designators of watts (W) to represent
instantaneous or average), volt-amperes-reactive (VARS) to represent reactive
volt-amperes (VA) to represent complex (or apparent) power.

 essentially a constant-speed motor when connected to a constant-

                          ducting central cores, becomes excessive.
 onductor configuration   Therefore,   to reduce the concentration of

                          phase is reduced, as is corona ionization

 lex Penetration Depth
eturn corrections have been carried out by using series-based
 of Carson’s infinite integrals (Carson, 1926). However, trunca-
cceptable for the impedances in cases with wide separation
  cy higher than power frequency, or low earth resistivity (Dom-
 eturn through homogeneous ground, the ground can be re-
placed below the ground surface at a distance p equal to the
                      complex penetration depth for plane
                      waves (Fig. 9.11). Such an approach has
                      been proposed in Dunbanton (1969),
                      Gary (1976), and Deri et al. (1981) and
                      produces results that match those ob-
                      tained from Carson’s correction terms.
                      The main advantage of this method is
                      that it allows use of simple formulae for
                      self and mutual impedances — formulae
                      derived from using the images of the
                      conductors — and, therefore, obtaining
                      accurate results through the use of elec-
                      tronic calculators.
                          The value of the complex penetration
                      depth in m is given by p  √/( j ),
                      where  is the ground resistivity in   m,
                      j is the imaginary number,  is the angu-
                      lar frequency in rad/s — equal to 377
                      rad/s for 60 Hz — , and       is the ground

                         2. Consider a Two-Conductor Line

                     between conductors, making it nonuniform.

e open delta, the flow-through three-phase kVA value is reduced to
 sed-delta value. The individual transformer loading is reduced to
o transformers that form the open delta as compared with 100 per-
 ransformers in a closed delta. The basic assumptions in these cal-
 ed symmetrical system of voltages and currents and negligible
s.

odels the nonlinear relationships among bus power injections,

  e heart of most system-planning studies and also the starting
namic stability studies. This section provides a formulation of
 d its associated solution strategies. An understanding of the
se systems is assumed, including per-unit calculations, complex
ircuit-analysis techniques.

 S) and the Newton-Raphson (N-R) Methods (Grainger and

  e it exhibits a faster convergence characteristic. However, the

 ng can oscillate without converging toward the solution. In or-

 ustry is currently undergoing major technological and organiza-
creasing presence of cost-effective, small, flexible power plants,
 lectronic control of wire equipment and the revolutionary changes
  computing all offer possibilities for active reliance on closed-loop
er systems. At the same time, the industry has moved from a top-
 sion making into active, decentralized decision making by the sys-
liers and users) with increased interest in minimizing systemwide
ent a power-systems-control designer with the need to revisit the
 system is operated today and to possibly establish new control
 ble to a decentralized operation.
 we provide a concise summary of the control design presently prac-
dustry first. We next describe the ongoing conceptual changes in the
design for the competitive industry. We emphasize conceptual issues
 other references related to specific designs and calculations neces-
 ontrollers for meeting the established performance criteria.

urbance(s) to Be Simulated
namic simulation is to predict the behavior of the system in response
 perturbation. This disturbance could be any possible change in the
ed to compute the initial steady state. Transient stability studies nor-
nces such as a fault of a specified type (e.g., single-phase to ground)
 f a generating unit, the false trip of a line, the sudden addition of a
  control input. This disturbance is normally modeled by a change in
 in the description of the various stability analyses.

uilibrium Condition
 e equilibrium condition is computed by setting all derivatives to
 nt dynamic model. In power systems, the equilibrium is normally
 dard power-flow routine. From this, the equilibrium condition is
 earlier for computing initial conditions. In either case, the equilib-

 r the new system condition. If the power flow fails to solve, the in-

 urve, the convergence may become a problem due to the ill-
obian matrix.

                    17.1
ation-plant cycle based on a steam turbine as the prime mover (STCP).
nt is a power plant that produces electrical power along with heat
steam flow or water flow (through installation of steam-water heat
 rial or residential consumption. The ratio of electric power to heat
 on the type of power plant. If the plant is located in an industrial
 ctive is often the supply of steam or hot water for industrial con-
 electric power output is considered as a byproduct and is relatively
 y companies have the inverse ratio of electric output to heat load,
considered as a byproduct.
nceptually different generation plant types. One is the steam-
ration plant (STCP) consisting of a steam turbine with the usual
 tion(s) for process steam supply (Fig. 17.1). The other is a gas-tur-
on plant (GTCP) consisting of one or more gas turbines exhausting
n through one or more heat-recovery steam generators (HRSGs),
or the heat supply (Fig. 17.2).
nt has the following major operational features: electric output in
  kJ (kcal, Btu); and heat rate in kJ/kWh (Btu/kWh). The cogener-
quires special definition. For a conventional power plant, heat rate
nsumption in kJ (kcal, Btu) per kilowatthour of electric output.
 n of heat rate is not applicable for cogeneration plants because it
 at output.

 t economical cogeneration-plant type — steam-turbine – based

  is the most important problem for the conceptual definition of
   o approaches to an optimization of the cogeneration plant:
namic analysis of STCP and GTCP, which represents a com-

 analysis, which is based on the evaluation of the present-worth
generation plant capital and operating costs for two cogenera-

 lants, information relevant to the costs of equipment and other
  ays available at the conceptual design phase.
 this section represent a first approach for the conceptual selec-
 nt cycle. Final selection is based upon more detailed calcula-
onsiderations such as water availability, environmental condi-
  l priorities, etc.

THE SULFURIC ACID (H2SO4)
TROLYTE
dards, such as the Uniform Fire Code, require reporting of the
 ery so that emergency responders know the hazards present in
 The electrolyte in a lead-acid battery is a solution of water and
by weight, of H2SO4 for different densities is provided in
